<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a0e59e71-77b2-4d52-aa08-2ea579e59d8b'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer1248031097199958103"><b>About three things I was absolutely certain.<br/>First, Edwart was most likely my soul mate, maybe.<br/>Second, there was a vampire part of him--which I assumed was wildly out of his control--that wanted me dead.<br/>And third, I unconditionally, irrevocably, impenetrably, heterogeneously, gynecologically, and disreputably wished he had kissed me.</b><br/><br/>And thus Belle Goose falls in love with t</span>
  <span id="freeText1248031097199958103" style="display:none"><b>About three things I was absolutely certain.<br />First, Edwart was most likely my soul mate, maybe.<br />Second, there was a vampire part of him--which I assumed was wildly out of his control--that wanted me dead.<br />And third, I unconditionally, irrevocably, impenetrably, heterogeneously, gynecologically, and disreputably wished he had kissed me.</b><br /><br />And thus Belle Goose falls in love with the mysterious and sparkly Edwart Mullen in the <i>Harvard Lampoon</i>’s hilarious send-up of Twilight. <br /><br />Pale and klutzy, Belle arrives in Switchblade, Oregon looking for adventure, or at least an undead classmate. She soon discovers Edwart, a super-hot computer nerd with zero interest in girls. After witnessing a number of strange events–Edwart leaves his tater tots untouched at lunch! Edwart saves her from a flying snowball!–Belle has a dramatic revelation: Edwart is a vampire. But how can she convince Edwart to bite her and transform her into his eternal bride, especially when he seems to find girls so repulsive?<br /><br />Complete with romance, danger, insufficient parental guardianship, creepy stalker-like behavior, and a vampire prom, <i>Nightlight</i> is the uproarious tale of a vampire-obsessed girl, looking for love in all the wrong places.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1248031097199958103" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/82065220" />
    <a title="Alli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1263249-alli"><img alt="Alli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1240723563p2/1263249.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/82065220?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alli" href="/user/show/1263249-alli">Alli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1263249-alli?shelf=books-2009">books-2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1263249-alli?shelf=books-2010">books-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1263249-alli?shelf=books-2012">books-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer82065220&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer82065220" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4358562939387035772">This was ABSOLUTELY hilarious. This is what everyone was (or should have been) thinking while reading the Twilight books.<br/><br/>There are conversations such as this:<br/><br/>Belle and her dad before Edwart picks her up: <i>"So, Belle, what's new today?"<br/><br/>"Dad," I said, grasping his hands and looking directly into his eyes. "I'm in the deepest love that has ever occurred in the history of the world."<br/><br/>"Gosh, Belle. When someone asks you, 'what's new?' the correct answer is, 'not much.' Besides, isn't it a little soon t</i></span>
  <span id="freeText4358562939387035772" style="display:none">This was ABSOLUTELY hilarious. This is what everyone was (or should have been) thinking while reading the Twilight books.<br /><br />There are conversations such as this:<br /><br />Belle and her dad before Edwart picks her up: <i>"So, Belle, what's new today?"<br /><br />"Dad," I said, grasping his hands and looking directly into his eyes. "I'm in the deepest love that has ever occurred in the history of the world."<br /><br />"Gosh, Belle. When someone asks you, 'what's new?' the correct answer is, 'not much.' Besides, isn't it a little soon to cut yourself off from the rest of your peers, depending on your boyfriend to satisfy your social needs as opposed to making friends? Imagine what would happen if something forced him to leave! I'm imagining pages and pages would happen- with nothing but the names of the month written on them!"</i><br /><br />and <br /><br /><i>I heard a knock on the door and breathed in sharply. How thoughtful of Edwart to knock when he could just as easily break down the door. I opened it expectantly.<br /><br />It was the mailman, grinning at me with that typical Switchblade smile.<br /><br />"Hi," he said. "Nice weather."<br /><br />I shifted awkwardly. I felt comfortable talking about a lot of things, but not the weather. I didn't quite have the terminology down, having skipped the grade in which you learn about various atmospheric conditions.<br /><br />"Yeah-the sun's on today," I guessed tentatively.<br /><br />"Well, you tell your dad I said hello."<br /><br />It was then that I finally understood. He was in love with me. It was all there-the doorbell ringing, the door stading, the showing off with his weather knowledge. Were there no other girls in this town to diffuse the responsibility of being loved?</i><br /><br />I read bits of this out loud to some friends as I was reading this, any time I found something funny, which would have me reading whole pages, and causing much hysterical laughter. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4358562939387035772" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText15370597359398529040" style="display:none">Not quite as terrible as I first thought, but still pretty bad. To give you some idea of what it's like, here's one of the passages I most enjoyed. Belle Goose is talking to her father:<blockquote>"So, Belle, what's new today?"<br /><br />"Dad," I said, grasping his hands and looking directly into his eyes. "I'm in the deepest love that has ever occurred in the history of the world."<br /><br />"Gosh, Belle. When someone asks you 'What's new?' the correct answer is 'Not much'. Besides, isn't it a little soon to cut yourself off from the rest of your peers, depending on a boyfriend to satisfy your social needs as opposed to making friends? Imagine what would happen if something forced that boy to leave! I'm imagining pages and pages would happen - with nothing but the names of the months on them."<br /><br />"If Edwart ever left, I'd find some other monster to hang out with. You know I have no social skills," I said. "I guess I'm like my dad in that way." I wasn't usually this emotional with him, and it felt good.</blockquote>Unfortunately, most of it isn't nearly as subtle and clever as that.<br /></span>

<div id="review_166188357" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/166188357" />
    <a title="Vinaya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya"><img alt="Vinaya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294127450p2/4687823.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/166188357?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vinaya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vinaya" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya">Vinaya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=books-i-liked">books-i-liked</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=twilight-spoof">twilight-spoof</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer166188357" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8825308228992837083"><i>I wiped the chemical dust off my clothes and sat down. Without looking at Edwart, I pulled out my textbook and notepad. Then, without looking at Edwart, I looked at the board and wrote down the terms Mr. Franklin had written. I don’t think other people in my situation could do quite so many things without looking at Edwart.<br/><br/>When the bell rang I stole another glance at him and shrank into a deeper sense of worthlessness. He was now staring furiously up at the bell, shaking all the muscles in his f</i></span>
  <span id="freeText8825308228992837083" style="display:none"><i>I wiped the chemical dust off my clothes and sat down. Without looking at Edwart, I pulled out my textbook and notepad. Then, without looking at Edwart, I looked at the board and wrote down the terms Mr. Franklin had written. I don’t think other people in my situation could do quite so many things without looking at Edwart.<br /><br />When the bell rang I stole another glance at him and shrank into a deeper sense of worthlessness. He was now staring furiously up at the bell, shaking all the muscles in his fist at it, glowering at it with his dark, heated eyes and loathing lashes. He clenched his hair in exasperation, clinging to the tussled tufts as he raised his head to the ceiling. Then he slowly turned to me. Looking into his eyes I felt waves of electricity, currents of electrons charging towards me. Was this how it felt to be in love, I wondered, for robots? Caught in his ionized hypnosis, the old adage came to mind:<b>Beautiful enough to kill, gut, stuff, and frame above your fireplace.</b></i><br /><br />Belle Goose is a catastrophically clumsy, scarily narcissistic teenager who has just moved to Switchblade to live with her father, a window-wiper, since her stepfather is going on tour with his street hockey team around Phoenix, and there may be no space for Belle to live in his car. <br /><br />Belle has a fascination with vampires, she believes her true love is destined to be one. When she spots the strange, lonely, barely-coherent Edwart Mullen in her new high school's cafeteria, she knows she's found her soul mate. <br /><br />Nightlight is funny, mostly. From the cover to the last page, this book is one large fart joke aimed at Twilight, and you can't help but find it hilarious. However, it gets a little old after a while. This is not a very long book, but after the first fifty pages of taking digs at Meyer's masterpiece, it begins to get repetitive. This is one of the main reasons I like satires better than spoofs. At least satires have a plot and actual characters. This is like a joke book - after the first fifty jokes, you want a break. <br /><br />There are some parts where the jokes are really funny, even subtle, and those made me laugh. However, you can pretty much tell from the preponderance of snot and body odor jokes that this was written by a bunch of smart-but-nerdy undergrads. <br /><br />Of course the end message, about judging by appearances, about building relationships on false illusions, about learning to love a person instead of an ideal, is one that every YA author ought to take home-<br /><br /><b>"We looked at each other and laughed a little because, hey, relationships take work, and communication."</b><br /><br />All in all, it's a quick entertaining read, but if you're expecting subtlety, class or major wit in your spoof, you're likely to be disappointed. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8825308228992837083" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_91622752" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/91622752" />
    <a title="Miffy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1389426-miffy"><img alt="Miffy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1267259779p2/1389426.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/91622752?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miffy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miffy" href="/user/show/1389426-miffy">Miffy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer91622752" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16744378432129667518">I love how people try to justify their bad reviews for this book by continuously stating that they do not like Twilight and that they are in fact true lovers of a parody. <br/>I really liked this book. But anything that takes piss out of this universal tragedy is a win. Some of the reviews here stated that the parody was 'too exaggerated,' 'overly obvious' etc. but I found it to be delightfully subtle; where minor details or single words effectively pinpoint the craptastic wonder of smeyer. <br/><br/>There wer</span>
  <span id="freeText16744378432129667518" style="display:none">I love how people try to justify their bad reviews for this book by continuously stating that they do not like Twilight and that they are in fact true lovers of a parody. <br />I really liked this book. But anything that takes piss out of this universal tragedy is a win. Some of the reviews here stated that the parody was 'too exaggerated,' 'overly obvious' etc. but I found it to be delightfully subtle; where minor details or single words effectively pinpoint the craptastic wonder of smeyer. <br /><br />There were some negatives about the parody. First was that my interest fluctuated throughout (I would be engaged one minute and then unattached the next). <br /><br />Second, it simply didn't hit hard enough. It was too soft on the twihards and the rest of the population in forcing them to realise that the this supposed 'best novel of all times' has the dead (and living) writhing in their graves. <br /><br />However the major con was the reader's realisation that a parody should never be better written (with a better plot and character development) than its original. Makes you lose hope for a little while...<br /><br />Will stop twi bashing now. Here is a widget that perfectly shows off smeyers pointless drivel of descriptions.<br /><br /><br />"I typed in a single word: Vampre. Google asked, "Did you mean 'vampire?'" I said, "Yes."</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15130476246089800662">It's hardly ground-breaking, but I'm giving it four stars on the sheer enjoyment factor. I'm actually a fan of the Twilight books, but I get that Stephenie Meyer is no Shakespeare and this series is hardly world class literature. <br/><br/>Twilight's gotten so huge it was only a matter of time before someone sent it up, so I was eager to see what a bunch of nerds from Harvard did to it.<br/><br/>Belle Goose is an exaggerated piss take of Bella.   <span id="freeText15130476246089800662" style="display:none">It's hardly ground-breaking, but I'm giving it four stars on the sheer enjoyment factor. I'm actually a fan of the Twilight books, but I get that Stephenie Meyer is no Shakespeare and this series is hardly world class literature. <br /><br />Twilight's gotten so huge it was only a matter of time before someone sent it up, so I was eager to see what a bunch of nerds from Harvard did to it.<br /><br />Belle Goose is an exaggerated piss take of Bella. She's self obsessed, and believes everyone else to be obsessed with her. Hmm... :L<br />The lovely Edwart is a girl phobic, Sega hating computer nerd who Belle falls for. I laughed out loud a lot during this book, but it felt as if it was a random collection of sentences lots of different people wrote. <br />Very confusing. I was expecting more of a 'Pride &amp; Prejudice &amp; Zombies' type thing, more of an exposé on all of the cheesy moments that make up Twilight, but it doesn't matter since the whole thing is the most non-serious thing I've ever read. =)<br /><br />Whether you like Twilight or believe Stephenie Meyer is the human form of Satan, Nightlight should bring you together through humour. A must-read. (:</span>

<div id="review_162203550" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/162203550" />
    <a title="Reading Teen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3329955-reading-teen"><img alt="Reading Teen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294347905p2/3329955.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reading Teen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reading Teen" href="/user/show/3329955-reading-teen">Reading Teen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer162203550" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6527982491215942295">Okay, so let me start with the fact that, yes, as shocking as it may be, I have read Twilight. So, after reading my review of this awesomely genius book, you can't use the excuse of, "You haven't read it, you don't understand!" I have read it. So, to all you Twilight fans, (And possible Harry Potter haters) I mean no disrespect in the following review. Your opinion is your own, and you are entitled to it.<br/><br/> TWILIGHT IS A HORRIBLE SERIES OF BOOKS.<br/><br/>Sorry. I had to let it out. So, now that you know my</span>
  <span id="freeText6527982491215942295" style="display:none">Okay, so let me start with the fact that, yes, as shocking as it may be, I have read Twilight. So, after reading my review of this awesomely genius book, you can't use the excuse of, "You haven't read it, you don't understand!" I have read it. So, to all you Twilight fans, (And possible Harry Potter haters) I mean no disrespect in the following review. Your opinion is your own, and you are entitled to it.<br /><br /> TWILIGHT IS A HORRIBLE SERIES OF BOOKS.<br /><br />Sorry. I had to let it out. So, now that you know my opinion of these books, you will understand my excitement when I discovered this book. There I was, rifling through a pile of books at a second hand book sale, and I stumbled across this wonderfully cool book. And let me tell you, it is... wonderfully cool.<br /><br />Alright, confession time. This isn't exactly my book. Abigaile, my sister, is the one who found and bought this book. So, my above statement is quite false. One day, I successfully stole it from her bedroom and, when she asked about it, convinced her that she had simply misplaced it. And, she believed me. Which was pretty surprising.<br /><br />Nightlight was an excellent parody to a not-so-awesome book. Belle Goose is actually really similar to the character Bella Swan. Pretty much everything Belle says in the book is just what Bella says at that moment in different words. It's completly hilarious to read and realize that this author is trying to make fun of this book when in reality he's just putting this book into different words, changing some plot details, and there you have it. A friggen' funny book.<br /><br />If you have read Twilight, watched the movies or know any thing at all about this sparkly-phenomanon, you will most likely love this book. Now, for you Twilight lovers out there, I honestly can't say. If you are the laid-back type of fan, it's a possibility that you will find this quite humorous. If you are a hard-core, Team-Edward/Team-Jacob kill-a-member-of-team-that-isn't-the-one-you-like type of fan (who is also easily offended) there might be a possible chance that you might not like this book, maybe. So... if you are one of those fans and you read this book and you hate it, I, Austin, am not responsible for this. So, you cannot do horribly awful things to me. Because Twilight may have sparkly vampiers, shirtless werewolves, and creepy human-vampier hybrids who age insanely fast, but us non-Muggles have wands, man-horses, cloaks that make you invisible, and Emma Watson.<br /><br />Edwart is right. Nintendo is better then Atari.<br /><br />Austin<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://ReadingTeen.net/">http://ReadingTeen.net/</a></span>

<div id="review_136444528" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/136444528" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3948070-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578088534p2/3948070.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/136444528?book_show_action=true">Dec 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/3948070-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer136444528" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7474683448700263798">This was a Christmas gift from my brother. He bought it for me because he “couldn’t remember which of those <i>Twilight</i> books you had already.” So sweet. And it’s a fitting gift from someone who only watches comedy and whose favorite TV show is “SNL.” <br/><br/><i>Nightlight</i> is a parody—you guessed it— of the first book in the <i>Twilight</i> series. It stars Belle Goose, who wants to be ‘turned’ and convinces herself that Edwart Mullen is actually a vampire who is thirsting for her blood and refuses to believe him wh</span>
  <span id="freeText7474683448700263798" style="display:none">This was a Christmas gift from my brother. He bought it for me because he “couldn’t remember which of those <i>Twilight</i> books you had already.” So sweet. And it’s a fitting gift from someone who only watches comedy and whose favorite TV show is “SNL.” <br /><br /><i>Nightlight</i> is a parody—you guessed it— of the first book in the <i>Twilight</i> series. It stars Belle Goose, who wants to be ‘turned’ and convinces herself that Edwart Mullen is actually a vampire who is thirsting for her blood and refuses to believe him when he tells her that he’s just a shy computer nerd/storm chaser/android builder. Misunderstandings and ridiculously narcissistic, strangely observant dialogue ensue. When Belle meets a real vampire, she must decide if the lifestyle is everything she’s fantasized it to be. (Twi-hards everywhere, take note: Belle Goose is a representation of <i>you</i>.)<br /><br />Some of my favorite moments:<br /><br /><b>“Belle,” he said. “It’s time to go.”<br />“Already?”<br />“It’s been five hours. We’ve been lying on the grass staring at each other for five hours. Please…I really need to get home.”</b><br /><br />--<br /><br /><b>It seemed out of place, coming from a girl in a sleeveless, lacy top and bell-bottom jeans (stars on the back pockets). But I was that kind of girl—out of place. Then I shifted from that place on the dashboard to a normal position in the seat. Much better.</b><br /><br />--<br /><br /><b>I typed in a single word: Vampre. Google asked, “Did you mean ‘vampire?’” I said, “yes.”</b><br /><br />--<br /><br /><b>“So, Belle, what’s new today?”<br />“Dad,” I said, grasping his hands and looking directly into his eyes. “I’m in the deepest love that has ever occurred in the history of the world.”<br />“Gosh, Belle. When someone asks you, ‘What’s new?’ the correct answer is, ‘not much.’”</b><br /><br /><br />This book was at its best when it directly satirized <i>Twilight</i>; the comedy got a little too Eggbert when it went on its own tangents. Need less to say, it would probably be most entertaining to those who have already read Stephenie Meyer’s series. It was dorky and stupid and really great fun. A quick, hilarious read. (Thank you again, S!) </span>
  <a data-text-id="7474683448700263798" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_206290198" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/206290198" />
    <a title="Cyna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4171731-cyna"><img alt="Cyna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356316087p2/4171731.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/206290198?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cyna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cyna" href="/user/show/4171731-cyna">Cyna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer206290198" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17469466867040491523">By far the more popular and more widely-available Twilight parody novel on the market, Nightlight was a huge disappointment. For a book written by the Harvard Lampoon - you know, IVY LEAGUE HUMOR PEOPLE - it's painfully dumb. Painfully. Perhaps it was my mistake for expecting something, I dunnno, more from them, but I went in to Nightlight hoping for some kind of relevant, witty commentary on Twilight's failures as a book. You know, jokes about the faults of its characters, the absurdities of th</span>
  <span id="freeText17469466867040491523" style="display:none">By far the more popular and more widely-available Twilight parody novel on the market, Nightlight was a huge disappointment. For a book written by the Harvard Lampoon - you know, IVY LEAGUE HUMOR PEOPLE - it's painfully dumb. Painfully. Perhaps it was my mistake for expecting something, I dunnno, more from them, but I went in to Nightlight hoping for some kind of relevant, witty commentary on Twilight's failures as a book. You know, jokes about the faults of its characters, the absurdities of the storyline, or lack there of. I expected something smart. In reality, the level of humor here can be accurately surmised by the monikers the Lampoon has bestowed on its lead characters. If you think Belle Goose and Edwart Mullen are downright HILARIOUS variations of Edward and Bella's names, then you may possibly find Nightlight funny. If, however, your reaction was closer to "Really? Is that the best you could come up with? Was that like...funny to you guys?" then you'd probably be better off avoiding it.<br /><br />It's a shame, too, because there were some amusing concepts and ideas presented in Nightlight that suffered terribly from skewed development. The idea is that Belle is delusional - she convinces herself that Edwart, your everyday unremarkable nerd, is a vampire because she wants him to be. Vampire boyfriends are cool, man, so she actively shoehorns him into that mold. Belle sees supernatural attributes where there clearly are none, and at points goes so far as to instruct Edwart in how to behave more like a vampire would. For example, she orders him to be more possessive and controlling of her - despite Edwart's obvious discomfort with it - because that's how vampires treat their girlfriends in the movies, hurhur. It's more a parody of the fangirl mentality than of Twilight itself, which could have worked fine, if more effort and intelligence had been put into it. Instead, aside from one or two amusing bits in the beginning re: Bella's mom, the Lampoon settles for nerd jokes and pratfalls rather than any meaningful satire.<br /><br />It's mind-boggling as to why, with a series as rife for parody as Twilight, the writers chose to take the delusional fangirl schtick and run it into the ground. If it weren't for the way the book mocks Stephenie Meyer's writing style, I'd wonder if the writers had even read Twilight at all, or if they'd simply settled for gathering their material from what they'd seen on tv and heard from their girlfriends and younger sisters. We get no kind of love triangle parody at all, which is absolutely absurd to me considering how much of Twilight, as a series, is devoted to that triangle, but how could we when there's not even a Jacob-equivalent character, if you can believe that. We really get no commentary on Bella's characterization except for her clumsiness, which is played often and loudly like she's a lost member of the Three Stooges, nor do we get any real parody of the increasingly ridiculous plot points throughout the Twilight series.<br /><br />Instead, at the last minute we get a random twist that involves Belle dating an actual vampire for a chapter or two, where she discovers the moral of the story: that dating an immortal asshole probably isn't all it's cracked up to be. Again, it's a nice idea, but aside from presenting said thesis in the most obvious way possible, that twist completely fizzles out and goes nowhere. Hell, even the Vampire Prom at the end - literally, a separate prom for vampires, probably the only joke that does garner a chuckle simply by existing - is wasted because they do nothing with it. It's just there. And for some reason, the authors have decided that things just being there is enough of a reason to laugh. And it's really not.<br /><br />Nightlight's saving grace is its brevity. At 150 pages, it's something you can breeze through in an hour, if you really feel like sticking with it that long. Personally, I'd say don't even bother with it at all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17469466867040491523" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3029488446012345287"><em>"It was then that I saw him. He was sitting at a table all by himself, not even eating. He had an entire tray of baked potatoes in front of him and still he did not touch a single one. How could a human have his pick of baked potatoes and resist them all? Even odder, he hadn't noticed me, Belle Goose, future Academy Award winner."</em><br/><br/>As a recovering Twilighter- wait, scratch that- as someone who can now see the Twilight series for what it really is- A very badly written hodge-podge of everything an </span>
  <span id="freeText3029488446012345287" style="display:none"><em>"It was then that I saw him. He was sitting at a table all by himself, not even eating. He had an entire tray of baked potatoes in front of him and still he did not touch a single one. How could a human have his pick of baked potatoes and resist them all? Even odder, he hadn't noticed me, Belle Goose, future Academy Award winner."</em><br /><br />As a recovering Twilighter- wait, scratch that- as someone who can now see the Twilight series for what it really is- A very badly written hodge-podge of everything an untalented "writer" ever read about vampires in OTHER AUTHORS' books, coupled with any Poor-Me-Teenage-Girl question and answer column out of Seventeen magazine, that took 4 books and half a million pages for something to happen and then it SUCKED- I needed to read this book.<br /><br />I cried, I screamed, I beat my fists against my pillow- and it was all because I was laughing so freaking hard I thought someone might mistakeningly commit me.<br /><br />It's absolutely ridiculous, stupid, disgusting and genius. I love how the description of Edwart's hair changed every time he was around. In this book we have Belle, a most loathsome character, just like Bella in <em>Twilight</em>. In <em>Twilight</em> Bella is pretty much unlovable and you really want to smack her but you can't quite put your finger on why- in <em>Nightlight</em> the reasons are painfully obvious. <br /><br />154 pages, you can read it in a minute, just don't read it in public- you might get locked up.</span>

  <span id="freeText10464850294452745364" style="display:none">This book was probably written by a bunch of drunk Lampoon employees at 2am. Then again, the book it's parodying reads like it was written in about 45 minutes by an unpopular 16-year-old girl who is dying to be part of the 'cool' crowd, so I suppose the authors got it bang-on with <i>Nightlight</i>.<br /><br />The reviews here panning this book make me laugh. Because <i>Twilight</i> is bad. It's very, very bad. It's poorly written (does the term 'thesaurus rapist' mean anything to you?), it's poorly plotted, and worst of all, it's rife with misogynistic innuendo. It's basically a how-to guide for creating and maintaining an abusive and co-dependent relationship in adolescence. <br /><br /><i>Nightlight</i> has hit the nail right on the head. Or driven the stake right through the heart. Oh, wait, I forgot! Vampires don't die from that anymore.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10453901460469035739">Now this book had me in laughing fits!<br/><br/>"About three things I was absolutely certain. First, Edwart was most likely my soul mate, maybe. <br/>Second, there was a vampire part of him-- which I assumed was wildly out of his control--that wanted me dead.<br/>And third, I unconditionally, irrevocably, impenetrably, heterogeneously, gynecologically, and disreputably wished he had kissed me."<br/><br/><br/>I picked up this book looking for a great laugh and boy did I get it. We meet Belle Goose, who leaves her mother and her ne</span>
  <span id="freeText10453901460469035739" style="display:none">Now this book had me in laughing fits!<br /><br />"About three things I was absolutely certain. First, Edwart was most likely my soul mate, maybe. <br />Second, there was a vampire part of him-- which I assumed was wildly out of his control--that wanted me dead.<br />And third, I unconditionally, irrevocably, impenetrably, heterogeneously, gynecologically, and disreputably wished he had kissed me."<br /><br /><br />I picked up this book looking for a great laugh and boy did I get it. We meet Belle Goose, who leaves her mother and her new stepdad Bill to move to Switchblade,Oregon with her father Jim. Who by was is a window-wiper. LOL. She goes to school and meets Edwart Mullen who is completely oblivious to Belle. He doesn't even like her. Belle falls a lot and into big things. She drives a U-HAUL truck to school taking up two parking spaces! I totally want to say more but I am afraid I will ruined it for those who want to read it. This book is a great read. It kept me laughing all day. My favorite part was when Belle added information to the wiki search she did on vampires:<br /><br /><br />"Then I thought, why don't I share my knowledge with the world? I sat back down at the computer and went to the vampire Wikipedia page. I added a sentence to the article: "Edwart Mullen of Switchblade, Oregon, is a vampire, but don't kill him because I love him!" Then I added a picture of Edwart's abs." <br /><br /><br />LOL! Seriously?<br /><br /><br /> Also it's a small book. It didn't take me more than an hour to read. As I did chores throughout the house, I kept thinking about what happen in the book and I would crack up. At one point, my husband found me laughing over the kitchen sink doing dishes and asked me "whats so funny" and I couldn't tell him because I couldn't breathe! He just shook his head at me and walked away. If your a fan of the Twilight series, this is a book you will enjoy.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10453901460469035739" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/2689336-ashley">Ashley</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81356895" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12274965556459893505">If you are a true "Twilight Saga" fan, then this book you will definitely add to your personal bookshelf.<br/><br/>Pros: With my weird sense of humor, I found this book to be absolutely comical. I laughed practically every other line, due to it's non-sensical-ness of the whole thing. This book displays some pretty funny truths of the "Twilight Saga", and in such a manner you can't do anything but agree. Fortunately, there IS some character development later in the book, and in the last chapter or so it br</span>
  <span id="freeText12274965556459893505" style="display:none">If you are a true "Twilight Saga" fan, then this book you will definitely add to your personal bookshelf.<br /><br />Pros: With my weird sense of humor, I found this book to be absolutely comical. I laughed practically every other line, due to it's non-sensical-ness of the whole thing. This book displays some pretty funny truths of the "Twilight Saga", and in such a manner you can't do anything but agree. Fortunately, there IS some character development later in the book, and in the last chapter or so it breaks away from the "Twilight" plot to come to it's own conclusion. This book also references other books, which I also found to be pretty humorous (maybe [HOPEFULLY:] they will add more parodies of this saga in the future?).<br /><br />Cons: As some reviewers have pointed out, this book can seem repetitive in it's writing style. Also, if you REALLY don't know the series (A.K.A you've only read through the series once, or you've only seen the movies), then this book will be downright confusing, weird, and not funny at all. Also, it's humor style is VERY random and different, so unless you can laugh at little things, it won't seem very funny at all.<br /><br />Judgement: If you have a "laugh-at-everything" sense of humor, are reading this book for pure enjoyment, and LOVE the Twilight Saga for what it really is (no, not the fangirl kind of love), then you will absolutely enjoy this book. 4/5 stars!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12274965556459893505" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Any and all Twilight lovers - It's pro-Twilight, I promise :|</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Fangirl Musings by: </span>
      My inner hatred
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1739253-fangirl-musings?shelf=classified-five-stars">classified-five-stars</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer133958722" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8077312506973635563">Kick ass to the extreme! The Twilight "saga" sucks...and here's proof! <br/><br/>By far, this parody was the single most comical, entertaining novella I've read in ages. In addition to the fact that it was written by the Harvard Lampoon, and is thus a tiny bit of demonstrative proof that smart people realize Meyer's Twilight book series is wretched literature, the comedy was very well done. Every negative aspect to the original series was addressed; the plot holes the size of China, the vomit inducing emo</span>
  <span id="freeText8077312506973635563" style="display:none">Kick ass to the extreme! The Twilight "saga" sucks...and here's proof! <br /><br />By far, this parody was the single most comical, entertaining novella I've read in ages. In addition to the fact that it was written by the Harvard Lampoon, and is thus a tiny bit of demonstrative proof that smart people realize Meyer's Twilight book series is wretched literature, the comedy was very well done. Every negative aspect to the original series was addressed; the plot holes the size of China, the vomit inducing emotional hyperbole, the transparently awful character creations, the lack of a cohesive, believable storyline, the plethora of grammatical errors, the overt evisceration of vampire lore, the death of originality...I could continue, but for the sake of wrapping up this run-on sentence, I'll refrain. <br /><br />Overall, Nightlight delivered a resounding triumph in giving me, the reader and avid Twilight hater, exactly what I wanted. I couldn't have asked for a better piece of humorous fiction even if I had it special ordered!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8077312506973635563" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_315519143" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/315519143" />
    <a title="Beaulah Pragg" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5738996-beaulah-pragg"><img alt="Beaulah Pragg" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518244257p2/5738996.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/315519143?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beaulah Pragg" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beaulah Pragg" href="/user/show/5738996-beaulah-pragg">Beaulah Pragg</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer315519143" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4143892882752761803">Humm.... this parody has the distinct flavour of one who was trying too hard. I found myself giggling at a rare moment of accidental humor, but the rest of the way was pretty hard going. Honestly, I think the authors sacrificed all attempts at coherence and plot for bizzare and often nonsensical gags. Edwart was probably the cutest character, with his nervous, geeky attempts at fulfilling Belle's yearning for a domineering 'dangerous' boyfriend. He honestly tried so hard... Which inevitably led </span>
  <span id="freeText4143892882752761803" style="display:none">Humm.... this parody has the distinct flavour of one who was trying too hard. I found myself giggling at a rare moment of accidental humor, but the rest of the way was pretty hard going. Honestly, I think the authors sacrificed all attempts at coherence and plot for bizzare and often nonsensical gags. Edwart was probably the cutest character, with his nervous, geeky attempts at fulfilling Belle's yearning for a domineering 'dangerous' boyfriend. He honestly tried so hard... Which inevitably led me to hating Belle. She was self-centred, deluded and incredibly annoying.<br /><br />What can I say? This 'parody' fell a bit flat except for the adorable, hilarious and oh so tragic character of dear Edwart. If they had just simplified and stuck with the idea of a girl who is addicted to the twilight series deciding that a boy in her class is a vampire, based on the 'obvious' signs, and then pursuing him relentlessly - and him trying so hard to please her because a girl has never been interested in him before... it would have been perfect. Get rid of all the try-hard humor that doesn't stick and parody the readers themselves. Who wouldn't want to read about a twilight-addicted school girl who thinks the class nerd is a vampire?</span>
  <a data-text-id="4143892882752761803" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78430065?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rhonda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rhonda" href="/user/show/699393-rhonda">Rhonda</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer835679813294005115">*giggles*<br/><br/>This is the tale of Belle Goose, a clumsy, self-important, day-dreaming girl from Arizona who moves to Switchblade, Oregon and falls for a brooding loner named Edwart Mullen. A vampire. Or is he?!<br/><br/>There were several times that this book made me laugh out loud. The endless description of how clumsy Belle is. The extremely negligent parenting. But her inner-monologue was my favorite. She constantly assumed that every boy wanted her, that everyone was talking about her or wanting to be her </span>
  <span id="freeText835679813294005115" style="display:none">*giggles*<br /><br />This is the tale of Belle Goose, a clumsy, self-important, day-dreaming girl from Arizona who moves to Switchblade, Oregon and falls for a brooding loner named Edwart Mullen. A vampire. Or is he?!<br /><br />There were several times that this book made me laugh out loud. The endless description of how clumsy Belle is. The extremely negligent parenting. But her inner-monologue was my favorite. She constantly assumed that every boy wanted her, that everyone was talking about her or wanting to be her or wishing she would talk to them. The self-centeredness was, ok not a <i>spot-on</i> parody, but it certainly made me snicker &amp; nod my head &amp; think, "see how ridiculous you are Bella?" (Yes, Bell<i>a</i> not Belle!)<br /><br />Here's my absolute favorite paragraph of the book, which illustrates probably my most hated moment from <i>Twilight</i>...or <i>New Moon</i> or whichever one it was from. It also captures the underlying theme of "I'm nothing without my man" that irked me so terribly about the whole series!<br /><br />"...isn't it a little soon to cut yourself off from the rest of your peers, depending on a boyfriend to satisfy your social needs as opposed to making friends? Imagine what would happen if something forced that boy to leave! I'm imagining pages and pages would happen - with nothing but the names of the month on them."<br /><br />It's comforting to know that Belle, for all her wackiness, makes the right choice in the end. :)<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="835679813294005115" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/146862942" />
    <a title="Mary Stevens" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4387987-mary-stevens"><img alt="Mary Stevens" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311884622p2/4387987.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/146862942?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary Stevens" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary Stevens" href="/user/show/4387987-mary-stevens">Mary Stevens</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Twilight-haters</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4387987-mary-stevens?shelf=misc">misc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer146862942" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer402554449627951744">To all you Twilight-haters out there, get ready for the best parody since "Epic Movie." <br/><br/>When Belle Goose moves to Switchblade, Oregon, she only expects one thing: to fall in love with a vampire and have him turn her into his immortal bride. So it's no surprise that, on her first day of school, she automatically suspects nonother than a Mr. Edwart Mullen to be her perfect match. After several incidents where Belle supposedly "roleplays," she finally realizes that he is not indeed a vampire... Wit</span>
  <span id="freeText402554449627951744" style="display:none">To all you Twilight-haters out there, get ready for the best parody since "Epic Movie." <br /><br />When Belle Goose moves to Switchblade, Oregon, she only expects one thing: to fall in love with a vampire and have him turn her into his immortal bride. So it's no surprise that, on her first day of school, she automatically suspects nonother than a Mr. Edwart Mullen to be her perfect match. After several incidents where Belle supposedly "roleplays," she finally realizes that he is not indeed a vampire... With the help of a REAL vampire named Josh. But after a distater of a prom, she realizes that she will only ever love Edwart. The book ends with them somewhat kissing, and leaving all Twihards sobbing into their hands.<br /><br />Me, on the other hand, laughed my butt off through the whole thing. I thought that it was well-written for a comedy, and had basically the same plotline Twilight. To me and my friends, we believed it was entirely the same (But more funny.) than Twilight. (Remember, this book is about 150 pages. Twilight is almost 500.) I believe that those geeks at Harvard finally did good in this world, and managed to create the best Twilight parody other than "Vampires Suck." My suggestion: Read it before 2012.</span>
  <a data-text-id="402554449627951744" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText2164426793284702934" style="display:none">So, a Twilight parody? Should be funny, right? And it was funny...just not as funny as I thought it would be. Still, worth reading if you are a Twilight fan who is willing to laugh a little at the series.<br /><br />Some of my favorite quotes:<br /><br />"About three things I was absolutely certain. First, Edwart was most likely my soul mate, maybe. Second, there was a vampire part of him -- which I assumed was wildly out of his control -- that wanted me dead. And third, I unconditionally, irrevocably, impenetrably, heterogeneously, gynecologically, and disreputably wished he has kissed me."<br /><br />"I imagined what I would be like after the transformation took place. I could probably wear leggings as pants every day, and no one would say anything because they would be afraid I'd bite them."<br /><br />"I should have known he wasn't a vampire. He failed to meet the three telltale criteria for vampirism: speaking in an old-timey way, being pompous, and having sparkly skin."</span>

<div id="review_163445056" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/163445056" />
    <a title="H.P. Holo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4961040-h-p-holo"><img alt="H.P. Holo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489445731p2/4961040.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/163445056?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="H.P. Holo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="H.P. Holo" href="/user/show/4961040-h-p-holo">H.P. Holo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer163445056" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7134591662136774580">I sit on the fence when it comes to 'Twilight' fandom; while there's a part of me that detests the series, there's another part of me that can read 200 pages of a 'Twilight' book in a single sitting, so I suppose there's a part of me that likes it, too. I'm also a lover of well-done parody, even of works that I legitimately do love, so I was rather excited to discover this book. However, while it is certainly a well-written parody, it is just as certainly not a well-done one. Let me clarify: The</span>
  <span id="freeText7134591662136774580" style="display:none">I sit on the fence when it comes to 'Twilight' fandom; while there's a part of me that detests the series, there's another part of me that can read 200 pages of a 'Twilight' book in a single sitting, so I suppose there's a part of me that likes it, too. I'm also a lover of well-done parody, even of works that I legitimately do love, so I was rather excited to discover this book. However, while it is certainly a well-written parody, it is just as certainly not a well-done one. Let me clarify: The writing style in this book is hilarious, and had it not been associated with 'Twilight,' it might have ended up being among my favorite works of recreationally witty literature. Its attempts to parody the 'Twilight' series are pointed but misguided. <br /><br />Bella in 'Twilight' is generally famous for being a romantic idiot; seeing that, the authors of 'Nightlight' opted to make their equivalent, Belle Goose, ridiculously and arrogantly intelligent--which might have worked, except that Belle Goose ends up being so different from Bella that she's hardly recognizable as a parody of said character. (The only way in which she is remotely similar is that, despite her brilliance, she does jump to some rather stupid conclusions about the parody's Edward, but even these are misguided.) The same goes for Edward--that is, Edwart--who, instead of being a vampire is, well, a gamer nerd who tires rather quickly of Belle assuming that he is a vampire. <br /><br />Story-wise, the book's one redeeming element is the end, in which Belle encounters some actual vampires who exist solely to satisfy all the readers exasperated with Bella's seeming love of being dominated by Edward; they show the dark side of that interest, something that 'Twilight' avoids in the name of romance. Despite its flaws, however, the novel does make for an entertaining read. It also possesses one benefit that 'Twilight' does not in that it's accessibly short, so even though I reached the end in indifference, I didn't feel as if I'd wasted much of my life. Read it if you need a distraction. Otherwise, make fun of 'Twilight' on your own; it may not sound as pretty, but it will probably be truer to the source material.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7134591662136774580" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_117211295" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/117211295" />
    <a title="Milena March" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2896173-milena-march"><img alt="Milena March" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1257003679p2/2896173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/117211295?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Milena March" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Milena March" href="/user/show/2896173-milena-march">Milena March</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Readers of Twilight, people looking for a light, quick read.</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer117211295&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer117211295" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6579190669206545102">Nightlight, a parody of Stephenie Meyer's hugely popular Twilight series, tells the story of the appropriately named Belle Goose who moves to the town of Switchblade and meets the mysterious and strangely attractive Edwart.<br/><br/>Not having read many perodies I wasn't quite sure what to expect; but as I'm not a fan of Twilight I felt it could only be enjoyable. Nightlight is good for a quick read; I finished it in a matter of hours.<br/><br/>There's no question that you really need to have read the Twilight seri</span>
  <span id="freeText6579190669206545102" style="display:none">Nightlight, a parody of Stephenie Meyer's hugely popular Twilight series, tells the story of the appropriately named Belle Goose who moves to the town of Switchblade and meets the mysterious and strangely attractive Edwart.<br /><br />Not having read many perodies I wasn't quite sure what to expect; but as I'm not a fan of Twilight I felt it could only be enjoyable. Nightlight is good for a quick read; I finished it in a matter of hours.<br /><br />There's no question that you really need to have read the Twilight series to appreciate most of the ridiculous things that happen in this parody. It helps, too, if you're aware of just how many ridiculous things happen in the original book. A few times in Nightlight I found myself thinking just how little I had realised some of the weaker points of Twilight which Nightlight rapidly picked up on. <br /><br />The unexpected ending - the appearance of the real vampire, Josh, and the escape of the 'fraud' Edwart - made me think more kindly on this at times disjointed and slightly dull book. Naturally, it does mirror the writing of the original books, but the ending made me think more kindly to it, highlighting one of the things that made me dislike the original Twilight series so much; the posessive characters of the vampires. Belle's return to Edwart seemed like the logical thing to do, despite the fact that he was, in fact, nothing more supernatural than a standard computer nerd. <br /><br />All in all, I think Nightlight just needs to be read with a grain of salt; it's good for a light, quick read, especially good if you're not a fan of the vampire romance genre.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6579190669206545102" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('VB7Ia6S45ioE7puKbECcRKAW4LuHczh5ZMgqEKA+Pip4JPLlunZwyhoK+S3VggCSMh/08E60d9MmJP6qebqxuQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('OAErTC7YUspMCLjThTJb9DGM6/8hPHbHt2+go3xoOJYUOxHCMBbEKlLs2nQ88Mcio4X/tOj7OW31g3QZpey3BQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Eine erlesene Mischung<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText15997038288628918164\" style=\"display:none\">Das ist ein Buch über \'die Beauvoir\', und Alice Schwarzer schöpft aus dem Vollen: viele Jahre der Freundschaft haben die beiden Frauen verbunden, und somit werden die 340 Seiten auch indirekt zu einem Buch über \'die Schwarzer\'. Eine erlesene Mischung aus ausgesuchten Texten, begleitenden Kommentaren und eigenen Gedanken. Die Klarheit ihres Denkens, die Unteilbarkeit ihres Gerechtigkeitssinnes und die Kühnheit ihrer Visionen, das sind drei der vielen Komplimente an Simone de Beauvoir, die Alice Schwarzer in ihrem Buch findet. Von der Frau, die in ihrem Leben alles wollte ist Alice Schwarzer nach wie vor hingerissen, wie Sie im Vorwort schreibt. Kein Wunder, sind es doch zwei Frauen, die mit der Ähnlichkeit ihrer Anliegen, ihres Engagements und ihrer Überzeugungen Vorbildcharakter hatten und haben, Kämpfernaturen waren und sind, und: sie haben Generationen beeinflusst. Beide plädierten und plädieren sie für uneingeschränkte Gleichberechtigung und das zu Zeiten, als es noch unerhört war. Die eine schon Jahrzehnte früher als die andere. Die ausgesuchten Texte, jeweils mit einleitenden Worten von Alice Schwarzer beinhalten die wichtigsten Kapitel der Beauvoir: In ihren Memoiren macht sie Station in ihrer Kindheit und Jugend, Ausschnitte aus Briefen an Sartre folgen und Kapitel aus dem Reisetagebuch ihres Amerika- Aufenthaltes. Dort war sie Ende der Vierziger Jahre bereits die bekannteste existentialistische Philosophin neben Sartre. Und es wird das Land der leidenschaftlichen Affäre mit dem Schriftsteller Nelson Algren. Auszüge aus Romanen, Erzählungen, Essays runden die Beauvoir- Palette ab. Ein unterhaltsames, klug komponiertes Porträt für die, die Simone de Beauvoire kennenlernen wollen und ein Buch für alle, die sie schätzen, immer wieder gerne lesen und erkennen, dass diese schillernde Französin keineswegs ihre Aktualität verloren hat. Als dieser sie betrügt, gelingt es ihr, den inneren Reichtum in würdige Stärke und Tätigkeit umzusetzen - und schließlich auch die gereifte Liebe ihres Mannes zurückzugewinnen.\n\nStifter verlegt die Lebens- und Leidensgeschichte Brigittas in die ungarische Steppe und schafft somit eine Verknüpfung des Schicksals seiner Protagonistin mit den politischen und kulturellen Geschehnissen in Ungarn.\n\nDie Novelle ›Brigitta‹ gehört zu den am häufigsten veröffentlichten und gelesenen Texten Adalbert Stifters. Wie bei nahezu all seinen Erzählungen existiert auch hier eine Ur- oder »Journal«-Fassung und eine Buchausgabe, in diesem Fall die sogenannte »Studien«-Fassung. Diese Edition enthält erstmals originalgetreu beide Versionen von 1844 und 1847 in einer parallelen Textanordnung.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"3469253304245327773\" href=\"#\" Getting it right won’t help if most everything else is wrong. And getting it wrong won’t hurt if most everything else is right. (There are countless books I cherish whose covers I don’t like too much, or cannot even now recall.) The interior of the book—the terrain of its pages, where all those words took me, the tiny but very real spot it ultimately occupies in my mind—that becomes the book. Next I go to the flaps. The front flap needs to intrigue/not bore me, and the bio needs to tell me just enough about the author. I’ll do my best to extract the author’s entire existence from their 2-X-2 inch photo.\n\nOff to the back cover. I’ll be momentarily impressed when I see a blurb by a hot writer like ____, but I know that it is just as likely that I’ll like the book as hate it regardless of these quotes. I look at them in a more voyeuristic way, like a literary gaper’s delay: Wow, the author knows So and So. Bet they send each other clever text messages. Really the only thing I can gauge from the blurbs is my own pathetic jealousy level.\n\nTo get a true sense of the book, I have to spend a minute inside. I’ll glance at the first couple pages, then flip to the middle, see if the language matches me somehow. It’s like dating, only with sentences. Some sentences, no matter how well-dressed or nice, just don’t do it for me. Others I click with instantly. It could be something as simple yet weirdly potent as a single word choice (tangerine).
